RE: Comments on General Plan Policies related to Historic Resources 
Dear Mayor Lee and City Council Members: 
Staff should be commended for their efforts on this complicated General Plan. We appreciate 
that many of our comments have been incorporated into the General Plan and are encouraged 
that the awareness of San Mateo’s  historic resources is increasing.   
RECOMMENDED CHANGES TO HISTORIC PRESERVATION POLICIES 
Summary 
Please consider these recommendations for the Community Design and Historic Preservation 
section of the General Plan. The proposed changes are further discussed below. 
1. Do not remove the word “eligible” from the historic policies. 
2. Add “in conformance with state and federal laws and CEQA” and “especially small 
businesses” to the new holistic approach policy. 
3. Add “or buildings” and “contributor properties to eligible historic districts” to the new 
Policy CD 5.1 Historic Preservation. 
4. Add “contributor properties to eligible historic districts” to the definition of historic 
resources in Policy CD 5.1 to ensure protection of historic districts. 
5. Add “(including contributors to historic districts)” to the definition of historic resources 
in Policy CD 5.3, to protect historic districts and be consistent with how Downtown 
historic resources are treated. 
6. Provide a reference or more information about the requirements of a historic resources 
report referenced in Policy CD 5.3. 
7. Add the requirement to identify demolition alternatives for contributors to a historic 
district. 
Change ID 5 New Policy 
Comprehensive Approach to Historic Preservation. Implement a comprehensive approach to historic 
preservation based on conformance with state and federal laws and CEQA, community input and best 
practices from State and federal agencies, to find the right balancing between preservation with other 
important priorities such as providing new homes and supporting local businesses, especially small 
businesses. 
352 of 445

--- page 353 ---
San Mateo City Council 
October 2, 2023 
Page 2 
 
 
 
A holistic approach is only a benefit if it follows state and federal laws and CEQA. Finding a 
balance between preservation and other important priorities can only occur if the City 
understands the resources that have already been lost (through a true cumulative impact 
analysis) and the remaining resources in the City (through surveys). The City should implement 
a moratorium on demolishing eligible historic properties until a cumulative impact analysis is 
completed through the Draft General Plan EIR.  
Change ID 6 Combined Policy CD 5.1 and 5.2  
Policy CD 5.1 Historic Preservation.   
Historic Preservation. Actively identify and preserve historic resources and concentrations of historic 
resources or buildings which convey the flavor of local historical periods, are culturally significant, or 
provide an atmosphere of exceptional architectural interest or integrity, or when they meet national, 
State, or local criteria. Historic resources include individual properties, districts, contributor properties 
to eligible historic districts, and sites that maintain San Mateo’s sense of place and special identity, and 
enrich our understanding of the city’s history and continuity with the past. 
Please add “or buildings” to reflect the definition of historic districts, which may consist of a 
group of buildings that are not individually eligible. Add “contributor properties to eligible 
historic districts” to ensure protection of historic districts, which often consist of a group of 
buildings that are not individually eligible, but are as a group.  
Policy CD 5.3: Historic Resources Definition.  
Define historic resources as buildings, structures, sites, and districts (including contributors to 
historic districts) that are listed in or determined to be eligible for listing in the National Register 
of Historic Places and/or California Register of Historical Resources, designated resources in the 
1989 Historic Building Survey Report, and resources found to be eligible through documentation 
in a historic resources report.  
Please add “contributors to eligible historic districts” to the definition of historic resources in 
Policy CD 5.3, to be consistent with how Downtown historic resources are treated. Contributors 
to historic districts must be protected in order to protect the integrity of the district. 
Please provide a reference or more information about the requirements of a historic resources 
report.  
Policy CD 5.7: Demolition Alternatives 
Please add the requirement to identify demolition alternatives for contributors to a historic 
district.  
Action CD 5.8: Historic Resources Context Statements, Action CD 5.9: Historic 
Resources Survey, and Action CD 5.10: Historic Preservation Ordinance 
Actions CD 5.8, 5.9, and 5.10 imply they will be conducted sequentially (Prepare neighborhood‐
specific historic context statements prior to updating the historic resources survey.) Please 
update the Historic Preservation Ordinance first to address the two new eligible historic 
353 of 445

--- page 354 ---
San Mateo City Council 
October 2, 2023 
Page 3 
 
 
 
districts (the Yoshiko Yamanouchi House Historic District and Baywood Historic District). The 
current historic ordinance seems to only apply to the Downtown Historic District (27.66.020 
APPLICABILITY). A first step to change the applicability of the ordinance to all of San Mateo. 
STAFF REPORT COMMENTS 
The staff report for the City Council meeting states on p. 5, under Community Feedback on 
Draft General Plan 2040, that there are emerging themes in feedback on the Draft General Plan. 
Two of the points are troubling: 
“… the emerging community feedback themes on the Draft General Plan, specific to the three elements 
being reviewed at this meeting, are as follows: 
Community Design and Historic Resources Element 
• Outline a process to designate a historic district that requires 2/3 approval of the affected 
property owners. 
• Do not designate new historic districts. 
Where did these points originate? The staff are calling out “Outline a process to designate a 
historic district that requires 2/3 approval of the affected property owners” and “do not 
designate new historic districts” as emerging themes, yet there were no such comments on the 
Notice of Preparation of the Draft General Plan EIR or on the Draft EIR. There were no such 
comments in the on‐line General Plan.   
I reviewed the comments on the General Plan and Draft EIR posted on the Strive website. There 
are many, many comments advocating for historic preservation. I did not see one comment that 
said: “require a 2/3 approval of the affected property owners” (taken from San Francisco 
policies which we do NOT want to emulate) or “do not designate new historic districts.” A 
September 26, 2023 letter refers to historic districts but does not accurately reflect the process of 
designation. The process is lengthy, complex, and determined by the State Office of Historic 
Preservation and the Keeper of the National Register of Historic Places (U.S. Park Service) based 
on detailed, objective criteria. Districts are not determined by “a small group of people.” In 
addition, the State will send a letter to the City and to each property owner in an eligible district 
asking whether the owner supports or objects to the district listing (a vote). The City has been 
informed of the Baywood Historic District process in every step but has declined to participate. 
PLANNING COMMISSION COMMENTS 
Commissioner Seema Patel has repeatedly misrepresented historic resources and the historic 
district process at public meetings and on social media. She falsely claims that an individual 
with enough time could determine eligible “hundreds or maybe thousands of properties or a 
handful of districts subject to additional restrictions” and maybe state laws without owner or 
staff or city consent—effectively losing local control. This is not how the process works. 
354 of 445

--- page 355 ---
San Mateo City Council 
October 2, 2023 
Page 4 
 
 
 
Commissioner Patel should know this, especially after claiming she has done extensive research 
on the topic. Her repeatedly promoting misinformation is behavior that is not appropriate for a 
City representative.  
PLANNING COMMISSION RECOMMENDATIONS 
We strongly object to the Planning Commission’s recommendation to remove “eligible” from 
the historic resources policies and actions. It is inappropriate for Planning Commissioners to 
advocate for acting in conflict with state and federal historic preservation laws and CEQA. Does 
this violate the oath taken by commissioners? This is another example of the Planning 
Commissioners acting in their own self‐interests (as a representative of the YIMBY Peninsula 
Advisory Board?) and ignoring the shared values of historic preservation and the community. 
Thank you for your consideration. 
 
Respectfully submitted, 
 
President 
San Mateo Heritage Alliance

Subject: Baywood 
  
  
 
Dear City Council members, 
  
My husband, David Goss and I, have lived in Baywood since 1985. We previously lived in the Aragon. We 
bought homes in these neighborhoods because of the beautiful architectural styles of the homes. We 
live at                   , which probably would be designated a historic resource in Baywood. We have 
remodeled our home in various ways over the years but have never even considered changing the front 
exterior of the home given its beautiful architecture. We fully support making Baywood a historic 
district. 
  
I am friends with Laurie Hieter.  I have known her since our kids started kindergarten at Baywood in 
1995. Laurie is much more knowledgeable than most about the ins and outs of making Baywood a 
historic district. I completely trust and agree with what Laurie is advocating about the wording of the 
historic preservation section of the general plan: 
  
1. Do not remove the word “eligible" from the historic policies. 
2. Add “contributors to eligible historic districts” to the definition of historic resources in 
Policy CD 5.3, to be consistent with how Downtown historic resources are treated and to 
protect historic neighborhood appearance. 
3.  Add the requirement to identify demolition alternatives for contributors to a historic 
district. 
4. Protecting historic resources is an important value in San Mateo and is compatible 
with adding affordable housing.  
  
  
Thank you, 
  
Peggy Berlese 
  
Best wishes, 
  
Peggy Berlese 
Herzig & Berlese

From: 
James Clark 
Sent on: Monday, October 2, 2023 8:47:11 PM 
To: 
Clerk <clerk@cityofsanmateo.org> 
CC: 
Zachary Dahl <zdahl@cityofsanmateo.org>; Somer 
Smith <ssmith@cityofsanmateo.org> 
Subject: Comment regarding 2040 San Mateo Plan 
  
  
 
Hello -  
 
I wanted to provide a comment on the San Mateo 2040 city plan, particularly around 
noise. My wife and I live along B street, along the section without traffic lights 
between 9th and 5th streets. Because of the larger street size here and the easier access 
to the freeway, we experience a lot of noise due to loud cars and Harley Davidson 
motorcycles racing up and down the street, often late at night. 
 
I've actually been in contact with local law enforcement on the issue, as late night 
parties at the Yuppie Bar / Cantina and the service staff at Espetus getting off work 
have recently become more problematic. I've also been sharing video footage that I've 
collected of a lot of bad behavior from repeat offenders who find it fun to race down 
what we now call the "San Mateo Speedway." 
 
My intention in all of this isn't to directly attack certain individuals or businesses, but 
more in a hope to effect some change in the way this section of San Mateo is 
designed. Given that there is currently a lot of pedestrian traffic through here (with 
more to come once a new project is built where Kelly Moore paints currently is), 
placing a few painted crosswalks is not going to stop this kind of behavior through 
here. Noise will simply increase while safety will decrease. 
 
We need to instead focus on various traffic calming measures to prevent the desire to 
speed and rev loud engines along B street in the first place. Occasionally sending 
officers out to ticket cars or to patrol sidewalks is not a sustainable solution 
unfortunately. Instead we should take simple measures like reducing street width sizes 
to specifically reduce the "open-ness" of the road that currently encourages this kind 
of behavior today.  
 
My hope would be to see permanent fixtures that slow and/or divert traffic included as 
part of the 2040 general plan for San Mateo. This could include tried-and-true city 
planning designs like raised intersections that not only slow cars but also provide 
better accessibility access, putting people first instead of optimizing for the speed and 
size of cars that are only getting faster and larger.  
357 of 445

--- page 358 ---
I believe with some relatively simple implementations of these designs applied as 
soon as is financially feasible (timed with repaving or other construction projects) will 
drastically increase the quality of life for those of us who live here in the wonderful 
city of San Mateo. 
 
Thank you. 
-James Clarke

From: 
linda lara < 
Sent on: Monday, October 2, 2023 9:33:31 PM 
To: 
City Council (San Mateo) <CityCouncil@cityofsanmateo.org> 
CC: 
                               ; San Mateo Heritage Alliance <info@smheritage.org> 
Subject: Tonight's CC Meeting - 10/2/23 
  
  
 
Dear City Council Members, City Manager and other city leaders,  
 
Regarding this evenings meeting about Draft General Plan 2040, 
please consider my thoughts as a long time resident of San Mateo since 1961. My 
daughter is now a 45 year resident of our city, with 3 children of her own. Generations 
of families live, work and play in our city and are creating their own history here. 
 
My comments in particular are about Historic Resources and maintaining them 
throughout our city either residentially, or commercially. 
 
Sadly, the City of San Mateo over many years has done little to preserve and maintain 
our historic resources and contributions made to our city and county by these historic 
resources. 
 
I'm not sure when the seemingly disregard for history began in our city, but in my 
estimation the first mistake was moving City Hall out of downtown to its present 
location. 
 
Little by little history is disappearing. 
Bay Meadows Race Track was a large contributor to the city and county of San 
Mateo, and to the best of my knowledge has received no historic recognition to date. 
 
Not only did they provide decades of revenue, they also provided jobs, recreation, 
sports and entertainment. 
Bay Meadows also remained open during WWII and contributed nearly 4 million 
dollars in war effort and hundreds of thousands of dollars to emergency war relief, 
veterans hospitals, wounded soldier funds, bay area army and navy bases etc. 
 
None of this seems to be acknowledged at the current Bay Meadows developments or 
anywhere throughout our city. 
 
In your plans for the future of this city, please, please do not erase it's past. 
Please find a way to embrace, promote, identify and tell the stories of our past history. 
 
361 of 445

--- page 362 ---
I am aware that the Ching Lee Laundry at 1st and Claremont has received a plaque 
and recognition. I do hope these efforts will continue throughout San Mateo. 
 
No one person should ever forget their beginnings, who they are, where they came 
from, how they grew and developed to who they are now. Nor should a city, county, 
state or country. 
 
Thank you for your time, thank you for listening. 
Sincerely, 
Linda Slocum Lara 
San Mateo Drive 
San Mateo

From:

Subject: Oppose Baywood Historic District 
  
  
 
I would like to take the opportunity to voice my opposition to a Baywood Historic District.  I received an 
email from supporters of the district asking for people to email the city council, so I am letting you know 
my opposing viewpoint. 
 
I believe that historic district designation is not warranted for a variety of reasons, many of which have 
been detailed by others.  Of course those wanting historical designation for their properties can pursue 
this now.  I would like to bring your attention to another argument against historic district designation, 
which is the history of racist restrictions in San Mateo property deeds.  The racist language remains 
despite a disclaimer, in my opinion precluding historical designation on that grounds alone. 
 
Thank you for your consideration, 
-Steve Miller

From: 
Maxine Terner  
Sent on: Monday, October 2, 2023 9:58:38 PM 
To: 
City Council (San Mateo) <CityCouncil@cityofsanmateo.org> 
CC: 
Alex Khojikian <akhojikian@cityofsanmateo.org> 
Subject: General Plan Update - Community Design and Historic Preservation Elements 
  
  
 
As a former Planning Commissioner knowledgeable about General Plans and someone who 
has actively participated in many of the General Plan update (GP) meetings, workshops and 
pop-up events, I am confused and concerned about the staff report and the unsubstantiated and 
seemingly biased language. Trust in government is fundamental to our democracy. 
 
Words matter. The Draft GP has NOT “focused on crafting a shared community vision for what 
San Mateo can be in the year 2040,” particularly with regard to selecting the preferred land use 
and circulation scenarios. The highest development land use scenario was NOT the 
“culmination of community, General Plan Subcommittee, and Planning Commission feedback” 
but that of the previous, pro-development City Council direction. The community’s vision for land 
use was clear when Measure Y passed which continued General Plan 2030. Tweaks to 
Measure Y were expected during the GP update but totally ignoring it was not.  
 
It must be pointed out that the number of people voting for Measure Y far surpassed the 
relatively few individuals participating in the GP update despite the expensive and extensive 
outreach so thoroughly enumerated in the staff report. Since the staff report relies so much on 
the “number” of outreach meetings, perhaps the Council should ask for an “outcome report” on 
how many unique individuals attended these meetings and whether their goals for inclusiveness 
and diversity were met. 
 
The report continues its confusing, biased and unsubstantiated language in referencing 
“themes.” Key themes on p.2 are identified broadly as: sustainability, environmental justice, 
and community engagement and addressed throughout the GP update.  Yet, on p.5 under 
Community Feedback it notes there are “emerging themes” in feedback on the Draft General 
Plan. What follows under the Community Design and Historic Resources Element is very un-
themelike, specific language that has not been previously seen nor discussed in any of the 
public meetings:  
 • Outline a process to designate a historic district that requires 2/3 approval of the affected 
property owners. 
 • Do not designate new historic districts.  
 
Who added this language and based on what? This language also conflicts with Attachment 
3, Recommended Staff Revisions # 5 and 6; and Big Ideas in GP 2040, Address Historic 
Preservation Holistically. Residents have consistently supported recognizing and protecting the 
unique historic resources of San Mateo. Many focus group participants in this and prior General 
Plans noted that the authentic downtown and traditional neighborhoods were reasons they 
moved to San Mateo. Historic Preservation policies have been part of the past two General 
Plans and should not be diluted in this one. Do not include this language in the Historic 
Resources Element. 
 
368 of 445

--- page 369 ---
My Specific Recommendations to Attachment 3, Revisions to the Community Design and 
Historic Preservation Elements follow: 
New Policy CD 5 - Add language:  Implement a comprehensive approach to historic 
preservation based on conformance with state and federal laws and CEQA, community 
input and best practices from State and federal agencies and to find the right balancing between 
preservation with other important priorities such as providing new homes and supporting local 
businesses, especially small businesses. 
 
Policy CD 8.3  Maintain language about “stepping back upper floors.”  This is especially 
important for taller buildings and consistent with many of the new higher height buildings built in 
neighboring Peninsula cities. It is also consistent with reducing wind and other impacts that 
conflict with having a pedestrian oriented downtown and community. 
 
Other Recommendations: 
1 - Prepare an “outcome report” on how many unique individuals attended all listed meetings 
and whether the Council's goals for inclusiveness and diversity were met. 
 
2 - Do not remove word "eligible" from Policy CD 5.3 as recommended by Planning Commission 
since it is legally required by state and federal laws, including CEQA. 
 
3 - Revise the public input schedule to give both the Council and residents adequate time to 
review and discuss the lengthy GP update. With the agenda packet going out late on a 
Thursday for input on a Monday, there is not enough time for residents to review. Especially 
when the staff report is so long and complex. There is no stated reason to rush for the 
November 2024 ballot; the existing GP is valid through 2030 and the Housing Element can be 
updated prior to then. 
  
Thank you for your consideration of these comments. We all share the goal of having a socially-
responsible GP 2040 that the community can be proud of and trust. 
 
Sincerely, 
Maxine

Dear City Council Members and City Manager, 
 
I have taken a close look at the Staff Report for tonight's 
10/2/23 City Council meeting, and I am submitting the 
following comments on items of specific concern. 
 
First, regarding the staff recommended revisions to the 
Historic Resources Element as outlined on Attachment 3, I 
encourage Council to consider adding the changes 
highlighted in yellow.  My reasoning follows in green 
italics. 
 
Change ID 5:  Add new policy to clearly support the City’s 
comprehensive approach to historic preservation. 
 
Comprehensive Approach to Historic Preservation. Implement a 
comprehensive approach to historic preservation based on conformance with state 
and federal laws and CEQA, community input and best practices from State and 
federal agencies, 
to find the right balancing between preservation with other important priorities such 
as providing new homes and supporting local businesses. 
 
State law, federal law and CEQA must provide the 
framework to this policy to ensure compliance. 
 
Change ID 6: Combine 2040 Draft General Plan Policies CD 5.1 and 5.2 to 
reduce redundancy. 
 
370 of 445

--- page 371 ---
Historic Preservation. Actively identify and preserve historic resources and 
concentrations of historic resources which convey the 
flavor of local historical periods, are culturally significant, 
or provide anatmosphere of exceptional architectural 
interest or integrity, when they meet national, State, or 
local criteria. Historic resources include individual 
properties, districts, contributor properties to eligible 
historic districts, and sites that maintain San 
Mateo’s sense of place and special identity, and enrich our 
understanding of the city’s history and continuity with the 
past. 
 
Contributor properties are very important components of 
an historical district.  As illustration, one can consider an 
historical district as a quilt made up of squares of both 
eligible individual properties as well as contributor 
properties.  All of them individually contribute to the whole, 
to the beauty, the identity, and character of the quilt. 
 
Secondly, I would also like to provide my comment on 
specific provisions of the Chapter 5 Community Design 
Historic Resources Draft and ask the Council to consider 
adding the following language highlighted: 
 
Policy CD 5.3: Historic Resources Definition. 
Define historic resources as buildings, structures, sites, and districts, including 
contributors to historic districts, that are listed in or determined to be eligible for 
listing in the National Register 
of Historic Places and/or California Register of Historical Resources, designated 
resources in the 1989 Historic Building Survey Report, and resources found to be 
eligible through documentation in a historic resources report. 
371 of 445

--- page 372 ---
Please add “contributors to eligible historic districts” to the definition of 
historic resources, for the same reasons I outlined above. 
 
Finally, I'd like to comment about the Planning 
Commission's feedback regarding the Historic Resources 
Element, specifically: 
 
Community Design and Historic Resources Element  
• Remove eligible as part of the definition of Historic Resources in Policy CD 5.3 
Historic Resources Definition.  
 
WORDS HAVE MEANING. STRIKING ONE LITTLE 
WORD CAN HAVE MAJOR CONSEQUENCES.  And I 
strongly object to the Planning Commission's 
recommendation to remove the word "eligible" from the 
definition of historic resources. That definition is critical to 
ALL provisions that follow in the Draft General Plan 
Historic Resources Element Goals, Actions and 
Policies.  Deleting that word not only has serious 
implications for the entirety of the Historic Resource 
Element, it also goes against State, Federal, and CEQA 
laws.  That our Planning Commission would advocate 
going against these laws should be of major concern to 
our City Council. 
 
Thank you for your time, and I sincerely hope my 
comments will be considered as you go forward in your 
deliberations this evening. 
 
Lisa Vande Voorde 
San Mateo Resident

Members of the San Mateo City Council: 
 
We have followed with great interest the development of the 2040 General Plan for 
the City San Mateo. 
 
The Draft General Plan is released and adoption appears to be imminent. 
 
There are many San Matins who strongly wish to preserve the “single family 
dwelling” aspect of our community.  
In view of the need for additional low income dwellings in California, and legislation 
which promotes the conversion of existing properties to multiple dwelling facilities, I 
feel that residents who live in or plan on living in San Mateo should have the choice 
to preserve single family homes in portions of our City. 
To that end, we feel that designating portions of San Mateo as Historic Resources is 
important. 
 
Please consider the following additions or changes to the 2040 General Plan: 
 
Add a requirement to identify “demolition alternatives” for homes that are identified 
as representing historic buildings; 
 
Add “contributors to eligible historic districts” to the definition of historic resources. 
 
Protecting historic resources is an important value in San Mateo, compatible with 
adding affordable housing, and acknowledges one reason that our family has chosen 
to live in San Mateo. 
 
Stephen A Awller, MD

Olds <polds@cityofsanmateo.org> 
Subject: San Mateo General Plan update - Goal COS-4 comment 
  
  
 
Dear Mayor Lee and Councilmembers, 
  
I am writing to you regarding the San Mateo General Plan 2040 update, further to my comments at the 
09/26 Planning Commission meeting on the same subject.  I want to support the staff-recommended 
change noted on Attachment 4 of your packet (page 258 of 259), regarding studying the feasibility of 
studying air pollution mitigations near highways, in areas where we are planning new housing.  
  
While the land rights and physical constraints along highway edges may appear to make this a daunting 
task, there are opportunities, including in our most highly polluted (in terms of carcinogenic diesel 
particulate matter) area, Study Area 8 at the confluence of US-101 and SR92.  For example, along South 
Amphlett Boulevard, the city should have room to fit screening and/or sound walls on city or private 
land.  These are both recommended by BAAQMD in their Planning Healthy Places guidance.  Please note 
– their #1 tool in this document is to not place new housing near heavily trafficked highways, but in the 
event that such is not feasible, they recommend these two approaches.  At this very high-level planning 
stage, I think it is appropriate to be consistent with our own contemplated goals and policies, including 
Goal LU-1 regarding environmental and health equity, and Policy LU 8.6 Safe and Sanitary Homes which 
says "Encourage homes and neighborhoods that are free of environmental health hazards." 
  
Thank you for your consideration, and for supporting a clean and safe San Mateo for current and future 
generations. 
  
Best, 
Martin Wiggins 
Planning Commissioner

Draft General Plan 2040 Key Themes
» Draft General Plan embodies three key themes which are 
woven throughout the document:
• Sustainability. Help ensure that San Mateo can meet its current needs 
and leave viable resources for future generations.
• Environmental Justice. Reduce the unique or compounded health risks in 
San Mateo’s equity priority communities.
• Community Engagement. Increase community participation in the 
planning and development processes

How the General Plan Will Be Implemented
» After adoption, City staff will work to implement 
the General Plan’s to-do list, or “Actions”
» Level of effort for each action varies: some are 
ongoing, some are one-time tasks

climate change risks
• Establish and maintain an inventory of historic resources
• Coordinate with Caltrain and SamTrans on transit 
improvements

each fiscal year

32
StriveSanMateo.org
of 59
CEQA Overview
» The California Environmental Quality Act (CEQA) is the State’s 
primary environmental protection law.
» An Environmental Impact Report (EIR) is an informational 
document:
•
Discloses the potential physical environmental impacts of projects
•
Identifies mitigation measures
•
Describes feasible project alternatives
» The EIR is the highest-level environmental review document under 
CEQA.
» CEQA does not dictate project approval or denial.
413 of 445

--- page 414 ---
33
StriveSanMateo.org
of 59
Program-Level EIR
"Program-level" EIRs are appropriate when a project consists of a 
series of actions related to issuing rules, regulations, and plans.
» Does not evaluate site-specific impacts of future projects that are 
consistent with the General Plan.
» Allows future project-level environmental review to "tier off" the 
program EIR.
» Streamlines future environmental review procedures.

of 59
Significant and Unavoidable Impacts
» Air Quality
• AQ-2: Construction of development projects that could occur from implementation of the proposed 
project would generate emissions that would exceed the Bay Area Air Quality Management 
District’s regional significance thresholds and cumulatively contribute to the nonattainment 
designations of the San Francisco Bay Area Air Basin.
• AQ-3: Operation of development projects under the proposed project would generate operational 
emissions that would exceed the Bay Area Air Quality Management District’s regional significance 
thresholds for volatile organic compounds (VOC) and nitrogen oxides (NOX).
• AQ-4: Construction emissions associated with development under the proposed project could 
expose air quality-sensitive receptors to substantial toxic air contaminant concentrations and 
exceed the Bay Area Air Quality Management District’s project-level and cumulative significance 
thresholds.
• AQ-6: Implementation of the proposed project would generate a substantial increase in emissions 
that exceeds the Bay Area Air Quality Management District’s significance thresholds and would 
cumulatively contribute to the nonattainment designations and health risk in the San Francisco 
Bay Area Air Basin.

36
StriveSanMateo.org
of 59
Significant and Unavoidable Impacts
» Noise
• NOISE-1: Buildout under the proposed project is anticipated to result in unacceptable traffic noise
with an increase of more than 5.0 dBA Ldn over existing conditions along one roadway segment
(1st Avenue west of B Street) within the EIR Study Area.
• NOISE-6: Buildout under the proposed project is anticipated to result in unacceptable cumulative 
traffic noise within the EIR Study Area.
» Wildfire
• WILD-2: Development under the proposed project would increase population, buildings, and 
infrastructure in wildfire-prone areas, thereby exacerbating wildfire risks.
• WILD-5: Potential development under the proposed project could, in combination with other 
surrounding and future projects in the State Responsibility Areas, Very High Fire Hazard Severity 
Zones, or Wildland Urban Interface, result in cumulative impacts associated with the exposure of 
project occupants to pollutant concentrations from a wildfire or uncontrolled spread of a wildfire 
due to slope, prevailing winds, or other factors.

37
StriveSanMateo.org
of 59
Cumulative Impact Findings
» Cumulative impacts account for development under the proposed 
project, in addition to other surrounding development, that could 
cumulatively cause an impact on the physical environment.
» The General Plan EIR is evaluated in the context of citywide 
cumulative impacts. 
» The Draft EIR finds that cumulatively considerable impacts could 
result from:
• Air Quality
• Noise
• Wildfire
418 of 445

--- page 419 ---
38
StriveSanMateo.org
of 59
Alternatives Analysis
» CEQA requires an EIR to describe a range of reasonable 
alternatives to the project that would attain most of the project 
objectives but would avoid or substantially lessen any of the 
project’s significant effects.
» One of the alternatives must be a “no project alternative.”
» The Draft EIR evaluates two alternatives: 
• No Project Alternative 
• Reduced Traffic Noise Alternative 
419 of 445

--- page 420 ---
39
StriveSanMateo.org
of 59
Statement of Overriding Considerations
The City may approve the project with significant and unavoidable 
impacts by issuing a “Statement of Overriding Considerations”
» Identifies how the project's benefits outweigh the potential impacts
• Examples: providing affordable housing, reducing per capita VMT, 
supporting local businesses
» Must be included in the record of project approval

“Policy COS 3.1 Aesthetic and Habitat Values - Public
Creeks. Preserve and enhance the aesthetic and habitat
values of creeks, such as San Matea, Laurel, and
Beresford Creeks, and other City owned channels in all

Recommended Change(s)

Policy COS 1.4 Avoidance of Nesting Birds. Native bird nests in
active use shall should be avoided when required by in compliance
with State and federal regulations. For new develapment sites
where nesting birds may be present, vegetation clearing and
construction should be initiated outside the bird nesting season
(March 1 through August 31) or preconstruction surveys should be
conducted by a qualified biologist in advance of any disturbance. If
active nests are encountered, appropriate buffer zones should be
established based on recommendations by the qualified biologist
and remain in place until any young birds have successfully left the
rest.

Policy COS 1.5 Surveys for Sensitive Natural Communities. Require
that sites with suitable natural habitat, including creek corridors
through urbanized areas, be surveyed for the presence or absence
of sensitive natural communities prior to development approval.
Such surveys shall should he conducted by a qualified biologist and
occur prior to development-related vegetation removal or other
habitat modifications.

Policy COS 1.6 Surveys for Regulated Waters. Require that sites with
suitable natural habitat, including creek corridors through
urbanized areas, be surveyed for the presence or absence of
regulated waters prior to development approval. Such surveys shall
shoule be conducted by a qualified wetland specialist and occur
prior to development-related vegetation removal or other habitat
modifications.

Policy COS 3.1 Aesthetic and Habitat Values — Public Creeks.
Preserve and enhance the aesthetic and habitat values of creeks,
such as San Mateo, Laurel, and Beresford Creeks, and other City
owned channels in all activities affecting these creeks, including
revegetation, rewilding, erosion contral, and adequate setbacks for
structures. Prioritize restoration of creeks and their riparian setback
as part of any new developments impacting the creeks.
